ozun deyis "import express, { type Request, Response, NextFunction } from "express";
import { registerRoutes } from "./routes";
import { setupVite, serveStatic, log } from "./vite";
import path from "path";

const app = express();
app.use(express.json());
app.use(express.urlencoded({ extended: false }));
app.use('/uploads', express.static(path.join(process.cwd(), 'uploads')));

app.use((req, res, next) => {
  const start = Date.now();
  const path = req.path;
  let capturedJsonResponse: Record<string, any> | undefined = undefined;

  const originalResJson = res.json;
  res.json = function (bodyJson, ...args) {
    capturedJsonResponse = bodyJson;
    return originalResJson.apply(res, [bodyJson, ...args]);
  };

  res.on("finish", () => {
    const duration = Date.now() - start;
    if (path.startsWith("/api")) {
      let logLine = ${req.method} ${path} ${res.statusCode} in ${duration}ms;
      if (capturedJsonResponse) {
        logLine +=  :: ${JSON.stringify(capturedJsonResponse)};
      }

      if (logLine.length > 80) {
        logLine = logLine.slice(0, 79) + "â€¦";
      }

      log(logLine);
    }
  });

  next();
});

(async () => {
  const server = await registerRoutes(app);

  app.use((err: any, _req: Request, res: Response, _next: NextFunction) => {
    const status = err.status || err.statusCode || 500;
    const message = err.message || "Internal Server Error";

    res.status(status).json({ message });
    throw err;
  });

  // importantly only setup vite in development and after
  // setting up all the other routes so the catch-all route
  // doesn't interfere with the other routes
  if (app.get("env") === "development") {
    await setupVite(app, server);
  } else {
    serveStatic(app);
  }

  // ALWAYS serve the app on port 5000
  // this serves both the API and the client.
  // It is the only port that is not firewalled.
  const port = 5000;
  server.listen({
    port,
    host: "0.0.0.0",
    reusePort: true,
  }, () => {

import express, { type Request, Response, NextFunction } from "express";
import { registerRoutes } from "./routes";
import { setupVite, serveStatic, log } from "./vite";
import path from "path";

const app = express();
app.use(express.json());
app.use(express.urlencoded({ extended: false }));
app.use('/uploads', express.static(path.join(process.cwd(), 'uploads')));

app.use((req, res, next) => {
  const start = Date.now();
  const path = req.path;
  let capturedJsonResponse: Record<string, any> | undefined = undefined;

  const originalResJson = res.json;
  res.json = function (bodyJson, ...args) {
    capturedJsonResponse = bodyJson;
    return originalResJson.apply(res, [bodyJson, ...args]);
  };

  res.on("finish", () => {
    const duration = Date.now() - start;
    if (path.startsWith("/api")) {
      let logLine = `${req.method} ${path} ${res.statusCode} in ${duration}ms`;
      if (capturedJsonResponse) {
        logLine += ` :: ${JSON.stringify(capturedJsonResponse)}`;
      }

      if (logLine.length > 80) {
        logLine = logLine.slice(0, 79) + "â€¦";
      }

      log(logLine);
    }
  });

  next();
});

(async () => {
  const server = await registerRoutes(app);

  app.use((err: any, _req: Request, res: Response, _next: NextFunction) => {
    const status = err.status || err.statusCode || 500;
    const message = err.message || "Internal Server Error";

    res.status(status).json({ message });
    throw err;
  });

  // importantly only setup vite in development and after
  // setting up all the other routes so the catch-all route
  // doesn't interfere with the other routes
  if (app.get("env") === "development") {
    await setupVite(app, server);
  } else {
    serveStatic(app);
  }

  // ALWAYS serve the app on port 5000
  // this serves both the API and the client.
  // It is the only port that is not firewalled.
  const port = 5000;
  server.listen({
    port,
    host: "localhost", // Changed from "0.0.0.0" to "localhost"
    reusePort: true,
  }, () => {
    log(`serving on port ${port}`);
  });
})();

import express, { type Request, Response, NextFunction } from "express";
import { registerRoutes } from "./routes";
import { setupVite, serveStatic, log } from "./vite";
import path from "path";

const app = express();
app.use(express.json());
app.use(express.urlencoded({ extended: false }));
app.use('/uploads', express.static(path.join(process.cwd(), 'uploads')));

app.use((req, res, next) => {
  const start = Date.now();
  const path = req.path;
  let capturedJsonResponse: Record<string, any> | undefined = undefined;

  const originalResJson = res.json;
  res.json = function (bodyJson, ...args) {
    capturedJsonResponse = bodyJson;
    return originalResJson.apply(res, [bodyJson, ...args]);
  };

  res.on("finish", () => {
    const duration = Date.now() - start;
    if (path.startsWith("/api")) {
      let logLine = ${req.method} ${path} ${res.statusCode} in ${duration}ms;
      if (capturedJsonResponse) {
        logLine +=  :: ${JSON.stringify(capturedJsonResponse)};
      }

      if (logLine.length > 80) {
        logLine = logLine.slice(0, 79) + "â€¦";
      }

      log(logLine);
    }
  });

  next();
});

(async () => {
  const server = await registerRoutes(app);

  app.use((err: any, _req: Request, res: Response, _next: NextFunction) => {
    const status = err.status || err.statusCode || 500;
    const message = err.message || "Internal Server Error";

    res.status(status).json({ message });
    throw err;
  });

  // importantly only setup vite in development and after
  // setting up all the other routes so the catch-all route
  // doesn't interfere with the other routes
  if (app.get("env") === "development") {
    await setupVite(app, server);
  } else {
    serveStatic(app);
  }

  // ALWAYS serve the app on port 5000
  // this serves both the API and the client.
  // It is the only port that is not firewalled.
  const port = 5000;
  server.listen({
    port,
    host: "localhost", // Changed from "0.0.0.0" to "localhost"
    reusePort: true,
  }, () => {
    log(serving on port ${port});
  });
})();

  const start = Date.now();
  const routePath = req.path;
  let capturedJsonResponse: Record<string, any> | undefined = undefined;

  const originalResJson = res.json;
  res.json = function (bodyJson, ...args) {
    capturedJsonResponse = bodyJson;
    return originalResJson.apply(res, [bodyJson, ...args]);
  };

  res.on("finish", () => {
    const duration = Date.now() - start;
    if (routePath.startsWith("/api")) {
      let logLine = `${req.method} ${routePath} ${res.statusCode} in ${duration}ms`;
      if (capturedJsonResponse) {
        logLine += ` :: ${JSON.stringify(capturedJsonResponse)}`;
      }

      if (logLine.length > 80) {
        logLine = logLine.slice(0, 79) + "â€¦";

      log(logLine);
    }
  });

  try {
    const server = await registerRoutes(app);

    app.use((err: any, _req: Request, res: Response, _next: NextFunction) => {
      const status = err.status || err.statusCode || 500;
      const message = err.message || "Internal Server Error";

      res.status(status).json({ message });

    });

    // Vite yalnÄ±z "development" rejimindÉ™ qurulur

      () => {
        log(`ğŸš€ Server running at http://${host}:${port}`);

â€‹The error message you're encountering, npm ERR! 404 Not Found - GET https://registry.npmjs.org/@types%2fvite - Not found, indicates that the package @types/vite is not available in the npm registry. This is because Vite provides its own TypeScript types, so there's no separate @types/vite package needed.â€‹

To resolve this issue, follow these steps:

Install Vite: Ensure that Vite is added as a development dependency in your project. You can do this by running:

bash
Copy
Edit
npm install --save-dev vite
or with Yarn:

bash
Copy
Edit
yarn add --dev vite
Configure TypeScript: Since Vite provides its own TypeScript types, you should include them in your tsconfig.json file. Add "vite/client" to the "types" array in your tsconfig.json to ensure TypeScript recognizes Vite's types:

json
Copy
Edit
{
  "compilerOptions": {
    // ... other options ...
    "types": ["node", "vite/client"]
  }
}
Clear npm Cache (If Necessary): If you've previously attempted to install @types/vite and are still encountering issues, it might be helpful to clear the npm cache:

bash
Copy
Edit
npm cache clean --force
Check npm Registry Configuration: Ensure that your npm is pointing to the correct registry. You can set it to the default npm registry using:

bash
Copy
Edit
npm config set registry https://registry.npmjs.org
Misconfigured registry settings can lead to 404 errors when attempting to install packages.

Verify Network Connectivity: Since you've previously encountered network-related errors, ensure that your internet connection is stable and that there are no firewalls or proxies blocking npm's access to the registry. You can verify connectivity by pinging the npm registry:

bash
Copy
Edit
ping registry.npmjs.org
A successful ping indicates that your machine can reach the npm registry.

By following these steps, you should be able to resolve the 404 error and continue with your project's setup. If you encounter further issues, consider consulting the npm documentation or seeking assistance from the npm community.

Install Missing Type Definitions: If you're receiving an error about a missing type definition for 'node', it's likely that the @types/node package isn't installed. To resolve this, run:â€‹

bash
Copy
Edit
npm install --save-dev @types/node
This command adds the Node.js type definitions to your project's development dependencies.

Configure tsconfig.json: Ensure that your tsconfig.json file is set up correctly to include the necessary type definitions. Add or verify the following settings:â€‹

Flavio Copes

json
Copy
Edit
{
  "compilerOptions": {
    "moduleResolution": "node",
    "types": ["node"]
  }
}
This configuration tells TypeScript to resolve modules using Node.js conventions and explicitly includes the Node.js types.

Check Module Paths: If you're encountering "Cannot find module" errors, it might be due to incorrect import paths or missing modules. Ensure that:â€‹
Stack Overflow

LambdaTest Community

Built In

The module you're trying to import is installed. For example, if you're importing express, make sure it's in your node_modules directory.â€‹

The import paths in your TypeScript files are correct and relative to the file's location.â€‹

The moduleResolution option in tsconfig.json is set to "node" to align with Node.js module resolution strategy.â€‹

bash
Copy

This removes the existing node_modules directory and reinstalls all dependencies as specified in your package.json.

Install TypeScript Locally: Ensure that TypeScript is installed locally in your project:â€‹

bash

Having TypeScript installed locally ensures that your project's build process uses the correct version.
